— other/historicaldocument —
[{'doc_type': 'pr',
  'num_of_pages': 2,
  'text': 'FDA NEWS RELEASE\n'
          'FOR IMMEDIATE RELEASE\n'
          '\n'
          'February 9, 2006\n'
          '\n'
          'Report Demonstrates Benefits of Earlier Meetings with FDA to Make '
          'Drug Review Process More\n'
          'Efficient\n'
          '\n'
          'The Food and Drug Administration (FDA) released a report that takes '
          'an in-depth look at the way the\n'
          'agency reviews applications for drugs and biologics that have not '
          'previously been approved by FDA. The\n'
          'report was commissioned to look at differences in applications '
          'approved by the agency during the first\n'
          'round of review (first-cycle) compared to those applications that '
          'took multiple reviews (multi-cycle)\n'
          'before approval. One of the most compelling findings was the '
          'positive impact "milestone meetings"\n'
          'held between a product sponsor and the FDA can have in making the '
          'drug review process more efficient\n'
          'by improving the quality of initial applications.\n'
          '\n'
          "The report, entitled Independent Evaluation of FDA's First Cycle "
          'Review Performance--Retrospective\n'
          'Analysis, showed the positive impact consulting with the FDA before '
          'beginning the final phase of human\n'
          'testing (end of Phase 2) can have on first-cycle approval rates. '
          'Fifty-two percent of companies that held\n'
          'a meeting with the FDA at the end of Phase 2 trials received '
          'approval during the first review cycle.\n'
          'However, only 29 percent of sponsors that did not have consultation '
          'meetings in this phase gained\n'
          'approval during the first review cycle for their product. In '
          'addition, the report also noted a positive link\n'
          'between a first-cycle approval and an earlier consultation before '
          'the application is even submitted -- of\n'
          '58 products with these types of meetings, almost half received '
          'first cycle approval.\n'
          '\n'
          '"These meetings have become one of the most valuable aspects of the '
          'drug development process," said\n'
          'Acting FDA Commissioner Andrew von Eschenbach, MD. "Earlier '
          'consultation and feedback from FDA on\n'
          "the sponsor's development program is critical to ensuring safe and "
          'effective study designs and\n'
          'increasing the probability that the resulting marketing application '
          'will meet regulatory requirements.\n'
          "These meetings are a unique aspect of FDA's review program, but "
          'they are very labor intensive and\n'
          'require adequate Agency resources in order to sustain the current '
          'success."\n'
          '\n'
          'Most products with multiple cycles had major deficiencies '
          'identified in only one or two areas.\n'
          'Deficiencies in safety assessment were the most common reason for '
          'FDA requesting additional cycles,\n'
          'followed by efficacy and chemistry/manufacturing related issues.\n'
          '\n'
          'The report also showed, however, that consulting with the FDA prior '
          'to application submission does not\n'
          'always prevent the need for multiple review cycles prior to '
          'approval. The report notes that even when\n'
          'major issues with an application are identified by FDA in milestone '
          'meetings, the sponsor did not always\n'
          'adequately address them prior to submission of the application. In '
          'fact, 71 percent of applications\n'
          'where key issues were identified by FDA during pre-submission '
          'meetings were not adequately resolved\n'
          'by the sponsor by the time of first action.\n'
          '\n'
          'As a result of this independent analysis the report recommends that '
          'in order to further improve first-\n'
          'cycle approval rates FDA should play a "much more proactive role" '
          'throughout the development\n'
          '\n'
          '\n'
          'process. The report suggests that this will help the agency to '
          'better work with the sponsor to identify\n'
          'and communicate issues and potential deficiencies earlier on in the '
          'review process. The report also\n'
          'recommended that the agency actively follow up with sponsors after '
          'milestone meetings to ensure the\n'
          'sponsor has adequately addressed issues identified during the '
          'meetings. The report notes, however,\n'
          'that implementing the recommendations would have significant '
          'resource implications for FDA given\n'
          'current workload and staffing in the reviewing divisions.\n'
          '\n'
          '"There has been dramatic growth in the number of meetings with '
          'sponsors in the past several years.\n'
          'The additional workload for meetings is going to have to be '
          'supported by additional staffing," said Dr.\n'
          "John Jenkins, Director of the FDA's Office of New Drugs in FDA's "
          'Center for Drug Evaluation and\n'
          'Research.\n'
          '\n'
          'More and more companies are seeking early advice from FDA. The '
          'independent report shows that\n'
          'increased communication with the FDA often results in a more '
          'informed and efficient drug development\n'
          'process, especially for products that represent a major innovation '
          'and have significant public health\n'
          'impact. Requests for consultations to review clinical milestones '
          'and next steps in the development\n'
          'process are up more than 60 percent over the past few years under '
          'PDUFA III. In fiscal year 2005, FDA\n'
          'received over 2,400 requests for formal meetings with industry on '
          'PDU FA products in development.\n'
          '\n'
          'The independent study was conducted by Booz, Allen Hamilton in '
          'relation to the Prescription Drug User\n'
          'Fee Amendments of 2002 (PDUFA III). This assessment includes a '
          'detailed evaluation of the events that\n'
          'occurred during the review process of new molecular entities for '
          'new drug applications (NMEs for\n'
          'NDAs), and biological license applications (BLAs) submitted in '
          'fiscal years 2002 to 2004.\n'
          '\n'
          "The study may be accessed on FDA's web site at: "
          'www.fda.gov/oc/pdufa/.\n'
          '\n',
  'year': 2006}]
